--- Commit Message ---
LU-13306 mgc: handle large NID formats

For newer versions of Lustre the MGS can send mgs_nidtbl_entry
containing NIDs of a larger format. Its also possible an old
MGS will send NIDs of the previous size. We need to handle
both cases. We reused the field of mcb_nm_cur_pass, which only
is used for nodemap, of the struct mgs_config_body to send the
NID size from the client to the MGS. Pre IPv6 clients will
by default have a zero mcb_nm_cur_pass / mcb_nid_size. When
mcb_nid_size is zero the the MGS will treat the client as
pre-IPv6 and send small NID back to the client. This avoids
needing to patch older clients. If the MGS is older then
small size NIDs will be sent back which the new MGC layer can
handle by converting those lnet_nid_t to struct lnet_nid.

To handle this new code the "swab" of the entry is split into
two parts. The "header" is "swab"ed as soon as we know the entry
is large enough for that to make sense. The content containing
NID information is swabbed later once the header has been found
to look sane.

Test-Parameters: serverversion=2.15 testlist=runtests,sanity,recovery-small

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-04-26 01:26:46.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

What is the point of this patch?
For master, we want to make lustre handle large nids, not gracefully ignore them.
So is this intended to be added to older releases so they can interoperate?
If so: making that explicit would help.

I had hoped that as mgs_nidtbl_entry contains nid_type and nid_size info, that unrecognized nids would be ignored.  I now see that isn't the case.  We should just fix those problems for a backport.
So:
 - lustre_swab_mgs_nidtbl_entry() should retrun when nid_type is not 0, rather then using LASSERT.
 - mgc_apply_recover_logs should either stop reading one it finds nid_type!=0 allowing previous entries to be used, or maybe skip over unknown types, as it has the size.

I think that is sufficient.
Your patch seems to do a lot more than that.  I certainly see no need to struct mgs_nidtbl_entry in older releases.
Am I missing something?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-04-27 00:22:57.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

> What is the point of this patch?
 > For master, we want to make lustre handle large nids,
 > not gracefully ignore them. So is this intended to be
 > added to older releases so they can interoperate?
 > If so: making that explicit would help.

I was thinking that this patch was splitting out the "compatibility" parts from patch https://review.whamcloud.com/50087 "LU-13306 obdclass: support large nids in mgs_nidtbl_entry" so that it could land to master (followed by a smaller 50087 that adds only the IPv6 NID handling) and also be backported to b2_15 and potentially b2_12 for older clients to be able to mount mixed-NID servers.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-04-28 17:46:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

Neil as Andreas pointed out we need a patch to back port to 2.15 LTS and maybe 2.12 LTS. Currently having an older client interactive with a newer MGS server will cause the client to fail to mount. With this patch it will not only work but even with large NIDs sent it will use the NIDs that are supported. A bonus is that I can also test this work with both an old style MGS (current) and with an MGS stack using larger NIDs.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-05-23 02:35:19.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

(1 comment)

Looks sensible - thanks.
I wonder if "nid_size" is the correct thing to be sending.  The nid size is already present in the information being sent, and the receiver if free to ignore what it doesn't like.
The purpose of the field is to work around a bug in older code which causes it to fail on things it doesn't recognise, rather than to ignore them.
So maybe "will_ignore_large_nids" is what we really want to say.  Or "no_bugs".

Maybe "nid_size" is OK .. it just doesn't seem quite right to me.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-05-31 17:19:20.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

We send the nid size info with struct mgs_nidtbl_entry which is sent from the MGS server to the client. The reserve is not the case. So I'm sending the nid size using struct mgs_config_body from the client to the MGS server. This informs us that it is safe to send larger NID sizes. With the size info we can filter and only send NIDs that the client can handle. This is in case struct lnet_nid expands in the future.

Now we could avoid this if we send NID strings instead which should always work. Andreas, Neil are you okay with this approach or would prefer using NID strings instead.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-06-05 06:16:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

> Patch Set 8:
> 
> We send the nid size info with struct mgs_nidtbl_entry which is sent from the MGS server to the client. The reserve is not the case. So I'm sending the nid size using struct mgs_config_body from the client to the MGS server. This informs us that it is safe to send larger NID sizes. With the size info we can filter and only send NIDs that the client can handle. This is in case struct lnet_nid expands in the future.

Hopefully all future code will be able to accept all NID sizes, and will quietly ignore anything that it is not able to handle.  So we should never need to change the nid size sent in mgs_config_body.

> 
> Now we could avoid this if we send NID strings instead which should always work. Andreas, Neil are you okay with this approach or would prefer using NID strings instead.

I prefer this approach rather than using NID strings.

Patch Set 13: Code-Review+1

(6 comments)

I think this is pretty good, and I like that the client request is sending the expected nid_size, since that makes it easier to figure out the limits in the future if it ever changes again.

I *do* think it makes sense to wire in OBD_CONNECT2_LARGE_NID at some point, but possibly not until the code is actually working before the 2.16 release and we can safely check that flag is sent by the clients and handled by the servers.
